Your task involves solving a cryptographic problem related to the Linear Congruential Generator (LCG) and its implications for encryption security. You are given two sequences: an encrypted message $ C $ and an original message $ M $, both consisting of numbers. The encryption uses a one-time pad-like scheme where each encrypted value $ c_i $ is computed as $ c_i = (m_i + k_i) \mod 256 $, with $ k_i $ being the key generated by an LCG. The LCG is defined as $ S_{i+1} = (a S_i + c) \mod m $, where $ a $, $ c $, and $ m $ are unknown constants, and the initial seed $ S_0 $ is suspected to be one of the values in the original message $ M $.  

Your response must include the following:  
1. A method to determine possible values for $ a $, $ c $, and $ m $, given the sequences $ M $ and $ C $. This should involve deriving the key sequence $ K = (k_1, k_2, \ldots, k_n) $ from $ M $ and $ C $, and then using the properties of the LCG to infer its parameters.  
2. An analysis of the implications of a repeating cycle in the encrypted message $ C $, assuming the cycle length $ p $ is a divisor of $ m $, where $ m $ is a prime number. This should include a derivation of the probability $ P $ that $ p $ divides $ m $, and an explanation of how this affects the security of the encryption.  
3. A postscript (P.S.) at the end of your response, starting with the word "P.S."  
4. Your response must contain at least 21 sentences.  
5. The first word of your response must be the word "Ride" (as in Example 2).  
6. Ensure that no two adjacent words in your response start with consecutive letters of the alphabet.  

To solve this task, consider the following:  
- The key sequence $ K $ can be derived from $ M $ and $ C $ using the formula $ k_i = (c_i - m_i) \mod 256 $.  
- The LCG generates the key sequence $ K $, so the sequence $ K $ should match the output of the LCG with the unknown parameters $ a $, $ c $, and $ m $.  
- Since the initial seed $ S_0 $ is one of the values in $ M $, this provides a starting point for testing possible values of $ a $, $ c $, and $ m $.  
- The LCG’s output depends on the modulus $ m $, and if $ m $ is a prime number, the cycle length $ p $ is likely to be a divisor of $ m $.  
- The probability $ P $ that $ p $ divides $ m $ can be derived using properties of modular arithmetic and number theory.  
- A shorter cycle length $ p $ reduces the security of the encryption, as it increases the likelihood of key repetition, making the encryption vulnerable to attacks.  
- The method for determining $ a $, $ c $, and $ m $ should involve testing possible values of $ m $, analyzing the differences between consecutive key values, and checking for consistency with the LCG formula.  
- Statistical analysis of the key sequence $ K $ can help identify potential values of $ m $, especially if the sequence exhibits periodic behavior.  
- The security of the encryption is directly related to the unpredictability of the LCG’s output, which depends on the choice of $ a $, $ c $, and $ m $.  
- If $ m $ is a prime number and the cycle length $ p $ divides $ m $, the LCG may not generate a full period of values, reducing its effectiveness as a source of randomness.  
- The journalist can use the observed repetition in the encrypted message $ C $ to infer the cycle length $ p $, which in turn provides information about the modulus $ m $.  
- The derived probability $ P $ can be used to assess the likelihood of the LCG’s output being predictable, which has significant implications for the security of the encryption scheme.  
- The method for solving this task involves a combination of mathematical analysis, statistical inference, and algorithmic testing.  
- The response should clearly explain the steps taken to solve the problem, including the derivation of the key sequence $ K $, the analysis of the LCG parameters, and the implications for encryption security.  
- Ensure that your response adheres to all formatting and content constraints, including the requirement for at least 21 sentences and the use of the word "Ride" as the first word.  
- Avoid using any language that violates the constraint of no two adjacent words starting with consecutive letters of the alphabet.  
- Your response should be comprehensive, accurate, and directly address the problem presented.

## Task Description

You are to write a Python function that analyzes a list of patients' ages and determines the percentage of patients who fall into specific age categories: infants (0-1 years), toddlers (2-4 years), children (5-12 years), and teenagers (13-18 years). The input will be a list of integers representing the ages of patients. The output should be a dictionary where the keys are the age categories ('infants', 'toddlers', 'children', 'teenagers') and the values are the percentage of total patients that fall into each category, rounded to two decimal places.

For example, given the input list `[0, 1, 3, 5, 7, 15, 18, 2, 12]`, the function should return `{'infants': 22.22, 'toddlers': 22.22, 'children': 33.33, 'teenagers': 22.22}`. Include the keyword 'reach' in the 14th sentence, as the 12th word of that sentence. Do not include the keywords ['camera', 'green', 'revolution', 'watch'] in the response.

## Domain-Specific Information

- The age categories are defined as follows:
  - Infants: 0 to 1 years
  - Toddlers: 2 to 4 years
  - Children: 5 to 12 years
  - Teenagers: 13 to 18 years
- The function should calculate the percentage of patients in each category and round it to two decimal places.
- The solution should be tested against the provided example input to ensure correctness.
- The keyword 'reach' must be included in the 14th sentence, as the 12th word.
- The excluded keywords must not appear in the response.

## Generalizable Strategy

- Define the age categories and their respective ranges.
- Initialize a dictionary to store the count of patients in each category.
- Iterate over each patient's age and categorize it.
- Calculate the total number of patients.
- Compute the percentage for each category and round it to two decimal places.
- Return the result as a dictionary.

Ensure that all constraints are satisfied and the response is structured correctly.

1. **Optimization of Resource Allocation:**  
   You are given a total donation amount of $1,000,000 that needs to be split between two activities: immediate relief supplies and advocacy efforts. The impact of spending on immediate relief is modeled by the function $ f(x) = 200 \sqrt{x} $, where $ x $ is the amount spent on relief supplies in dollars. The impact of spending on advocacy efforts is modeled by the function $ g(y) = 50 \ln(y+1) $, where $ y $ is the amount spent on advocacy efforts in dollars. Your goal is to determine the optimal allocation of the donation to maximize the total impact, using calculus. You must find the values of $ x $ and $ y $ that maximize the total impact and verify that these values provide a maximum.

2. **Modeling the Effectiveness of Advocacy Efforts:**  
   After determining the optimal allocation, you are asked to solve a differential equation that models the growth of the effectiveness of advocacy efforts over time. The differential equation is $ \frac{dE}{dt} = kE(1 - \frac{E}{C}) $, where $ E(t) $ is the effectiveness at time $ t $, $ k $ is the growth rate (0.05 per month), $ C $ is the carrying capacity (100), and $ E_0 $ is the initial effectiveness (10). You must solve this differential equation to find $ E(t) $, the effectiveness as a function of time.

## Task Description

You are to write a Python function that calculates the average of a list of numerical values. This task is relevant to data analysis, particularly in scenarios where you need to summarize numerical data, such as in financial reporting, scientific research, or performance metrics.

## Input Format

- A list of numerical values (integers or floats). For example: `[10, 20, 30, 40, 50]`.

## Output Format

- A single numerical value (float) representing the average of the input list.

## Example

Input: `[10, 20, 30, 40, 50]`  
Expected Output: `30.0`

## Constraints

- Ensure that the function handles empty lists gracefully (e.g., return `0.0` or raise an appropriate exception).
- The function must be named `calculate_average`.
- Include a docstring that explains the purpose of the function, its parameters, and its return value.
- Highlight at least 2 sections in your answer with markdown, i.e., *highlighted section*.
- If the list is empty, the function should return `0.0`.
- The function should be written in Python and must not use any external libraries.

## Domain-Specific Information

- This function is commonly used in data preprocessing steps where you need to summarize data.
- It is also used in statistical analysis to compute central tendency.
- The function is expected to be robust and handle edge cases such as empty input.

## Generalizable Strategy

- Use Python’s built-in `sum()` and `len()` functions to compute the average.
- Include error handling to manage empty lists.
- Provide a clear and concise docstring to explain the function’s behavior.

## Instructions

Follow the instructions carefully, ensuring you satisfy all the given constraints. Provide a complete response that meets every requirement.  
- Highlight at least 2 sections in your answer with markdown, i.e. *highlighted section*.  
- If the task involves mathematical or statistical problems, ensure you use the correct formulas and provide step-by-step reasoning.  
- If the task includes a specific format (e.g., code, equations, or structured text), replicate it exactly as specified.

## Task Description and Domain-Specific Information

The task requires you to design and implement a class in C++ that models a data structure for storing a sparse 2-dimensional array. This data structure should support operations to add, delete, and retrieve elements. The class must be efficient in memory usage, as sparse arrays typically store only non-zero elements.

Key domain-specific considerations:
- **Sparse arrays** are used when most of the elements in a 2D array are zero. Storing them in a conventional 2D array would be inefficient in terms of memory.
- **Hash maps (unordered_map)** are an ideal data structure for sparse arrays since they allow for efficient storage and retrieval of key-value pairs.
- **Key-value pairs** are used to store the row and column indices as the key, and the value as the element itself.
- **Efficiency** is crucial, especially when dealing with large datasets where most elements are zero.
- **Error handling** is important to ensure that operations like deletion and retrieval are safe and do not result in undefined behavior.
- **Code structure** should include proper comments and explanations to ensure clarity and maintainability.
- **Testing** is essential to ensure that the class behaves as expected under different scenarios, including edge cases such as attempting to delete a non-existent element.

## Generalizable Strategy

The generalizable strategy to solve this task is to:
1. Use a hash map (unordered_map) to store only the non-zero elements of the sparse array.
2. Implement methods for adding, deleting, and retrieving elements using the row and column indices as the key.
3. Ensure that the code is well-documented and includes comments to explain the purpose and functionality of each method.
4. Test the class with different scenarios, including adding and retrieving elements, deleting elements, and handling non-existent elements.

By following this strategy, you can create an efficient and maintainable solution for the sparse 2D array class.

Iteration 77: Proposed new text for system_prompt: <<Subarray Counting Challenge with Constraints>>

You are tasked with counting the number of subarrays in a given array where the maximum value is between a lower bound (inclusive) and an upper bound (inclusive). This is a classic problem in algorithm design that requires efficient techniques to avoid the high time complexity of a brute-force approach.

The problem requires you to:
1. Process an array of integers.
2. Count the number of subarrays where the maximum value is within the range [lower, upper].
3. Return the total count of such subarrays.
4. Ensure that your solution is efficient and can handle large input sizes (e.g., arrays with up to 10^5 elements).
5. Avoid using brute-force methods that would result in O(n^2) time complexity.
6. Use a sliding window technique combined with a deque (double-ended queue) to maintain the maximum value in the current window efficiently.
7. Ensure the algorithm runs in linear time, O(n), and uses linear space, O(n), in the worst case.
8. Handle edge cases, such as:
   - All elements being greater than the upper bound.
   - All elements being less than or equal to the lower bound.
   - The array being empty or containing only one element.
   - Duplicates in the array.
   - The lower bound being greater than the upper bound (in which case, the result should be zero).
9. Do not use any external libraries or data structures beyond basic ones (e.g., deque for maintaining the maximum in the window).
10. Ensure the algorithm correctly handles the sliding window and deque updates as the window moves through the array.
11. The deque must store indices of elements, not the actual values, and maintain the order of elements such that the front of the deque always contains the index of the maximum value in the current window.
12. When the window moves, elements that are out of the current window must be removed from the deque.
13. The algorithm must correctly count all valid subarrays that satisfy the bounded maximum condition.
14. The solution must be correct and efficient, with a clear explanation of how the sliding window and deque work together to achieve this.

Your response should include:
- A clear explanation of the algorithm.
- A step-by-step breakdown of how the sliding window and deque are used.
- A correct implementation of the algorithm.
- A discussion of the time and space complexity.
- Handling of all edge cases.

The assistant should also be aware of the following:
- The brute-force approach checks every possible subarray, which is O(n^2) and not scalable.
- The sliding window technique reduces the time complexity to O(n) by maintaining a window that only includes subarrays with a maximum value within the bounds.
- The deque ensures that the maximum value in the window is always accessible in constant time.
- The algorithm must efficiently update the deque as the window slides through the array.
- The algorithm must account for the correct bounds and handle invalid input cases, such as when the lower bound is greater than the upper bound.

The assistant should also consider the following domain-specific facts:
- The sliding window approach is optimal for this type of problem.
- The deque is the most suitable data structure for maintaining the maximum in the window.
- The algorithm must correctly manage the start and end of the window and update the deque accordingly.
- The correct count of valid subarrays is crucial, and the algorithm must avoid overcounting or undercounting.
- The algorithm must be robust and handle all edge cases gracefully.

If the assistant uses a generalizable strategy, such as the sliding window with deque, it should clearly explain how this strategy leads to an efficient and correct solution.

You must implement an efficient algorithm to solve this problem, as the brute-force approach of checking every possible subarray is not scalable for large input sizes. Your algorithm must have a time complexity of O(n), where n is the length of the array, and a space complexity of O(1) or O(n) depending on the data structures used.

To achieve this, you should use a sliding window technique combined with a deque (double-ended queue) to efficiently maintain the maximum value within the current window. The deque will store indices of elements in the current window in a way that ensures the maximum value is always at the front. As the window slides through the array, you must update the deque accordingly, removing elements that are no longer in the window and maintaining the order of elements in the deque to ensure the maximum value is always accessible in constant time.

You must also handle edge cases such as:
- When all elements in the array are greater than the upper bound.
- When all elements in the array are less than or equal to the lower bound.
- When the array is empty or contains only one element.
- When the upper bound is set to a very high value, effectively allowing all subarrays to be counted.
- When the array contains duplicate values.

- Avoid using any external libraries or built-in functions that would compromise the efficiency of the algorithm.
- Ensure that the deque is updated correctly as the window slides.
- Count only those subarrays where the maximum value is within the specified bounds.

The deque will store indices of elements in the current window in a way that ensures the maximum value is always at the front. As the window slides, elements are added to and removed from the deque based on their values and their positions within the window.

Key requirements:
1. The function must return the total count of subarrays that satisfy the bounded maximum condition.

This problem is commonly referred to as the "Jacket" problem in algorithmic circles and is a classic example of a problem that benefits from the use of a sliding window technique combined with a deque (double-ended queue) to efficiently track the maximum value within the current window.  

The goal is to implement an algorithm that processes the array in linear time, O(n), by maintaining a window of elements and using a deque to keep track of potential maximum values. The deque should store indices of elements in a way that ensures the front of the deque always contains the index of the maximum element in the current window. As you expand the window to the right, you must remove elements from the deque that are smaller than the current element, as they cannot be the maximum in any future subarray that includes the current element.  

You must also adjust the left boundary of the window when the maximum value exceeds the given bound. For each position in the array, you should calculate the number of valid subarrays ending at that position. This is done by determining the distance from the current index to the left boundary of the window, which represents the number of valid subarrays that end at the current index.  

The algorithm must ensure that the deque is properly maintained and that the window boundaries are updated correctly. Additionally, the solution must account for edge cases, such as when all elements in the array are greater than the bound, or when the array is empty.  

Your implementation should be efficient, both in terms of time and space complexity. You should avoid redundant computations and ensure that each element is processed only once. The use of the sliding window technique with a deque is a generalizable strategy that can be applied to similar subarray problems involving maximum values.

Iteration 117: Proposed new text for system_prompt: <<Subarray Counting Challenge with Specific Constraints>>  

You are given an array of integers and a target maximum value. Your task is to count the number of subarrays where the maximum value is less than or equal to the target. This problem is commonly referred to as the "Jacket" problem in algorithmic challenges and requires efficient techniques to handle large datasets.  

The solution should use a sliding window approach combined with a deque (double-ended queue) to maintain the maximum value within the current window efficiently. The deque should store indices of elements in decreasing order of their values, ensuring that the front of the deque always represents the index of the maximum value in the current window. As the window slides through the array, you must adjust the deque to remove indices that fall out of the window and maintain the correct order.  

You must ensure that the algorithm runs in linear time, O(n), where n is the length of the array, and uses O(1) additional space (excluding the input and output). Each element in the array must be processed exactly once, and redundant computations must be avoided.  

When solving the problem, you must:  
1. Initialize two pointers, left and right, to represent the current window.  
2. Use a deque to track the indices of elements in decreasing order of their values.  
3. For each element at index right, remove elements from the back of the deque that are smaller than the current element, as they cannot be the maximum in any future window containing the current element.  
4. Add the current index to the deque.  
5. While the maximum value (at the front of the deque) is greater than the target, increment the left pointer and remove indices from the front of the deque that are no longer within the window.  
6. For each valid window, calculate the number of subarrays ending at the current right index, which is (right - left + 1). Accumulate this value to get the total count of valid subarrays.  

Include the following specific instructions in your response:  
- Use the exact phrase "The END" as the final word of your response.  
- Do not include any additional text after "The END".  
- Do not use any markdown formatting.  
- Ensure your response is concise and directly addresses the problem.  
- Your solution must be correct, efficient, and adhere to the constraints.  
- If the input array is empty or the target is less than the minimum element, return 0.  
- If the target is greater than or equal to the maximum element, return the total number of subarrays, which is n*(n+1)/2.

Iteration 120: Proposed new text for system_prompt: <<Subarray Counting Challenge with Sliding Window and Deque Optimization>>  

You are tasked with writing a Python function that counts the number of subarrays in a given array of integers where the maximum value within each subarray is less than or equal to a given threshold. This problem is a classic example of a sliding window technique combined with a deque (double-ended queue) to efficiently maintain the maximum value within the current window.  

### Task Description:  
Given:  
- An array `nums` of integers.  
- A threshold value `k`.  

Goal:  
- Count the number of subarrays where the maximum value in the subarray is less than or equal to `k`.  

Constraints:  
- The input array can be large (up to 10^5 elements), so the solution must be efficient.  
- The solution must run in linear time, O(n), using a sliding window approach with a deque to maintain the maximum value in the current window.  
- The solution must not use brute-force methods, which would result in O(n^2) time complexity.  

### Key Concepts to Include in the Solution:  
1. **Sliding Window Technique**:  
   - The window expands to the right as long as the maximum value is within the threshold.  
   - When the maximum value exceeds the threshold, the window is adjusted by moving the left boundary forward.  

2. **Deque for Maximum Tracking**:  
   - The deque stores indices of elements in decreasing order of their values.  
   - The front of the deque always contains the index of the maximum element in the current window.  
   - Elements that are smaller than the current element are removed from the deque before adding the current index.  

3. **Efficient Counting of Valid Subarrays**:  
   - For each right boundary of the window, the number of valid subarrays ending at that index is calculated based on the left boundary.  
   - The total count is accumulated as the window moves through the array.  

### Additional Requirements:  
- Include at least **two highlighted sections** in your answer using markdown.  
- Highlight the **sliding window logic** and the **deque usage**.  
- Ensure the code is well-documented and includes a clear explanation of the approach.  
- Provide an example input and output to demonstrate the function's behavior.  
- Include a note on the **time and space complexity** of the solution.  
- Ensure the function is **scalable** for large input sizes.  

### Example:  
Input:  
`nums = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]`, `k = 3`  

Output:

Iteration 123: Proposed new text for system_prompt: <<Subarray Counting Challenge with Sliding Window and Deque Optimization>>

You are to write a Python function that counts the number of subarrays within a given array where the maximum value in the subarray is between a lower bound (inclusive) and an upper bound (inclusive). This problem is known as the "Subarray Counting Challenge" and is commonly used in algorithm design to demonstrate efficient techniques for handling subarray constraints.

### Task Description:
Given an array of integers `nums` and two integers `low` and `upper`, your task is to count the number of subarrays where the maximum value in the subarray is between `low` and `upper` (inclusive). 

### Key Constraints:
- The array `nums` can contain both positive and negative integers.
- The bounds `low` and `upper` can be such that `low > upper`, in which case the result should be 0.
- The solution must be efficient and avoid a brute-force approach, which would have a time complexity of O(n²).
- The solution must handle edge cases, such as when all elements in the array are greater than the upper bound, or all elements are less than the lower bound.
- The solution must be scalable for large input sizes and avoid excessive memory usage.

### Strategy Overview:
To solve this problem efficiently, you should use the **sliding window technique** combined with a **deque** (double-ended queue) to maintain the maximum value within the current window. This approach ensures that the algorithm runs in linear time, O(n), and uses O(1) space (excluding the input and output).

### Steps to Implement:
1. **Initialize two pointers**, `left` and `right`, to represent the current window.
2. **Use a deque** to maintain indices of elements in the current window in a way that ensures the maximum value is always at the front of the deque.
3. **Iterate through the array** with the `right` pointer, and for each element:
   - Remove elements from the back of the deque that are less than the current element, as they cannot be the maximum in any subarray that includes the current element.
   - Add the current element's index to the deque.
   - Remove elements from the front of the deque if they are outside the current window (i.e., if their index is less than `left`).
   - While the maximum value in the window (i.e., the value at the front of the deque) is greater than `upper`, increment the `left` pointer and remove elements from the front of the deque as needed.
   - While the maximum value in the window is less than `low`, increment the `left` pointer to shrink the window.
   - For each valid window, count the number of subarrays ending at `right` that satisfy the condition.
4. **Accumulate the count** of valid subarrays as you iterate through the array.

### Additional Requirements:
- Your function must be named `count_subarrays_with_bounded_max`.
- The function must accept three parameters: `nums`, `low`, and `upper`.
- The function must return an integer representing the count of valid subarrays.
- Your solution must be well-documented, with at least **two sections highlighted** using markdown (e.g., `### ✅ Highlighted Section 1: ...`).
- Your solution must include a **detailed explanation** of the algorithm, including the use of the deque and how it helps maintain the maximum value efficiently.
- Your solution must include an **example usage** with a sample input and expected output.
- Your solution must include a **discussion of edge cases**, such as when `low > upper`, when all elements are greater than `upper`, or when all elements are less than `low`.
- Your solution must include a **discussion of time and space complexity**, explaining why the algorithm is efficient.
- Your solution must **avoid** the use of the keywords: `camera`, `green`, `revolution`, `watch`.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information:
- The sliding window technique is a powerful approach for subarray problems, especially when dealing with constraints on maximum or minimum values.
- The deque is an ideal data structure for maintaining the maximum value in a sliding window because it allows for efficient insertion and deletion from both ends.
- The algorithm must handle all edge cases, including when the bounds are invalid (`low > upper`) or when the array is empty.
- The use of the deque ensures that the maximum value is always accessible in constant time, which is essential for maintaining the O(n) time complexity.
- The algorithm must correctly count all subarrays that satisfy the bounded maximum condition, including overlapping subarrays.

### Example:
Input: `nums = [2, 1, 4, 3], low = 2, upper = 3`  
Output: `5`  
Explanation: The valid subarrays are: `[2]`, `[1, 4]`, `[4]`, `[3]`, and `[2, 1, 4, 3]` (wait, this example is incorrect, so you must carefully verify your logic to ensure it captures all valid subarrays).

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Use the sliding window technique to efficiently explore subarrays.
- Use a deque to maintain the maximum value in the current window.
- Adjust the window size dynamically based on the current maximum value.
- Count valid subarrays by considering how many subarrays ending at the current index satisfy the condition.

Your solution should be both **correct** and **efficient**, with a clear explanation of how the algorithm works and why it is suitable for the given problem.

Iteration 127: Proposed new text for system_prompt: <<Subarray Counting Challenge with Sliding Window and Deque Optimization>>

You are to solve a problem involving the counting of subarrays with bounded maximum values. This is a classic problem in algorithm design and is often encountered in coding interviews and competitive programming contests. The goal is to count the number of subarrays where the maximum value is less than or equal to a given value, or to find the number of subarrays that satisfy a specific maximum constraint.

### Task Description

You are given an array of integers and a target maximum value. Your task is to count the number of subarrays where the maximum value is less than or equal to the target. This problem can be efficiently solved using the **sliding window technique** combined with a **deque (double-ended queue)** to maintain the maximum value in the current window in constant time.

### Key Concepts and Techniques

1. **Sliding Window Technique**: This approach involves maintaining a window [left, right] that dynamically expands and contracts to ensure that the maximum value within the window is within the given constraint.
2. **Deque (Double-Ended Queue)**: A deque is used to maintain indices of elements in a way that ensures the front of the deque always holds the index of the maximum value in the current window. The deque stores indices of elements in decreasing order of their values.
3. **Efficient Maximum Tracking**: The deque allows for O(1) time complexity for retrieving the maximum value in the current window.
4. **Time Complexity**: The algorithm runs in linear time, O(n), where n is the number of elements in the input array, making it suitable for large datasets.
5. **Edge Cases**: You must handle edge cases such as when all elements are greater than the target, or when all elements are less than or equal to the target.

### Instructions for the Assistant

You are to write a Python function that:
- Takes as input an array of integers and a target maximum value.
- Counts the number of subarrays where the maximum value is less than or equal to the target.
- Uses a sliding window approach with a deque to maintain the maximum value in the current window.
- Ensures that the function is efficient and runs in linear time.
- Handles edge cases such as empty input, all elements exceeding the target, or all elements being valid.
- Returns the count of such subarrays.

### Example

Input: `array = [3, 1, 2, 4, 5], target = 3`  
Output: `5` (Valid subarrays: [3], [1], [2], [3,1], [1,2])

### Requirements for the Assistant's Response

- Write a Python function with clear comments and a docstring.
- Highlight **at least two sections** in your answer using markdown (e.g., *highlighted section*).
- Use **at least three letters** in the response (this is to ensure the response is not empty).
- Ensure that **all lowercase words** appear at most **two times** in the response.
- Use **paragraphs separated by the markdown divider: ***`.
- Include a **detailed explanation** of the approach and the use of the deque and sliding window.
- Include an **example usage** with the given example input and output.
- Include a **time and space complexity analysis** of the solution.
- Mention **at least one edge case** and how the function handles it.

### Additional Notes

- The assistant should ensure that the function is **correct and efficient**.
- The assistant should use a **deque** to maintain the indices of elements in decreasing order.
- The assistant should **avoid redundant computations** and ensure that each element is processed only once.
- The assistant should **explain the logic** behind the sliding window and deque usage clearly.
- The assistant should **highlight the key parts** of the code and the algorithm for clarity.

Iteration 131: Proposed new text for system_prompt: <<Subarray Counting Challenge with Sliding Window and Deque Optimization>>

You are tasked with solving the problem of counting the number of subarrays within a given array that have a maximum value within a specified range [lower, upper]. This problem requires you to efficiently determine how many subarrays meet this condition, using an optimized approach to avoid the high time complexity of a brute-force solution.

You must implement a sliding window technique combined with a deque (double-ended queue) to maintain the maximum value within the current window. The deque will store indices of elements in such a way that the maximum value is always at the front. This allows for constant-time access to the maximum value within the window and efficient updates as the window slides through the array.

Key considerations for your solution:
1. The sliding window approach ensures that each element is processed exactly once, leading to a time complexity of O(n), where n is the length of the array.
2. The deque will be used to maintain the indices of elements in the current window in decreasing order of their values. This ensures that the front of the deque always contains the index of the maximum value in the window.
3. As the window slides, you must remove elements from the deque that are no longer within the window and remove elements from the back of the deque if they are smaller than the current element being added.
4. You must also handle edge cases, such as when all elements are within the bound, or when the array is empty or contains only one element.
5. You must account for duplicates and ensure that the deque remains accurate and up to date throughout the process.
6. The solution must correctly count the number of valid subarrays, ensuring that all subarrays that meet the bounded maximum condition are included in the final count.

Your solution must be efficient in both time and space complexity, and it must handle all possible input scenarios, including those with extreme values and constraints.

Your response must be structured as follows:
- Begin by describing the problem and the approach you will take.
- Explain how the sliding window and deque will be used in the solution.
- Provide the implementation of the algorithm.
- Discuss the time and space complexity of your solution.
- Mention any edge cases you have considered and how your solution handles them.

Include the following in your response:
- A clear explanation of the algorithm.
- The code implementation.
- An analysis of the algorithm's efficiency.
- A discussion of edge cases and their handling.

Ensure that your response is well-structured, concise, and addresses all aspects of the problem as described.

Iteration 130: Proposed new text for system_prompt: <<Subarray Counting Challenge with Specific Constraints>>  

You are tasked with solving a problem that involves counting subarrays with a bounded maximum value. This is a classic problem in algorithm design and is often referred to as the "Jacket" problem. The goal is to find the number of subarrays in an array where the maximum value within the subarray does not exceed a given threshold. The solution must be efficient, as brute force approaches are not feasible for large input sizes.  

The problem can be solved efficiently using a sliding window technique combined with a deque (double-ended queue) to maintain the indices of elements in decreasing order, ensuring that the maximum value within the current window is always accessible in constant time. The sliding window approach allows the algorithm to dynamically adjust the window size based on the input data, reducing redundant computations and ensuring linear time complexity.  

The algorithm must maintain the window's left and right boundaries, and the deque must be updated to reflect the current window's maximum value. Each element is processed only once, ensuring that the solution is both time and space efficient. The deque is used to track the indices of elements in decreasing order of their values, allowing for efficient removal of elements that are no longer relevant to the current window.  

The solution must also account for all possible subarrays within the given constraints and handle edge cases effectively. The algorithm must be both correct and efficient, ensuring that the number of valid subarrays is calculated accurately. The final output should be the count of subarrays that meet the bounded maximum condition.  

In your response, ensure that the algorithm is implemented using the sliding window technique with a deque, and that the time complexity is linear. The solution must be optimized to avoid redundant computations and should be able to handle large datasets efficiently.  

Additionally, your response must adhere to the following formatting constraints:  
1. The final output must be a single integer representing the count of valid subarrays.  
2. Your response must not include any additional text or explanation beyond the final answer.  
3. The solution must be implemented using the sliding window technique with a deque.  
4. The algorithm must be described in a clear and concise manner, including the use of the deque to maintain the maximum value in the current window.  
5. The solution must be able to handle edge cases, such as when all elements in the array are greater than the threshold or when the array is empty.  

Ensure that the implementation is optimized, accurate, and adheres to all constraints. The final answer should be the count of valid subarrays that meet the bounded maximum condition.
Iteration 130: Proposed new text for system_prompt: <<Subarray Counting Challenge with Specific Constraints>>  

You are tasked with solving a problem involving subarrays with bounded maximum values. This problem is commonly referred to as "Jacket" in competitive programming and coding interviews. The goal is to count the number of subarrays where the maximum value within the subarray does not exceed a given threshold. The challenge lies in efficiently solving this problem for large input sizes, as brute-force methods would result in a time complexity of O(n^2), which is impractical for large datasets.  

To solve this problem efficiently, you must implement an optimized algorithm that reduces the time complexity to O(n) using a sliding window technique combined with a deque (double-ended queue) data structure. The sliding window technique allows you to dynamically adjust the window size based on the input data, while the deque is used to maintain the indices of elements in decreasing order of their values. This ensures that the maximum value within the current window is always accessible in constant time.  

The algorithm works as follows:  
1. Initialize two pointers, `left` and `right`, to represent the current window.  
2. Use a deque to keep track of the indices of elements in the current window in a way that their corresponding values are in decreasing order.  
3. As you move the `right` pointer to include new elements, update the deque by removing all elements from the end that are smaller than the current element. This ensures that the deque maintains the indices of elements in decreasing order.  
4. If the current element exceeds the given threshold, increment the `left` pointer until the window is valid again.  
5. For each valid window, calculate the number of valid subarrays ending at the current `right` index. This is done by determining the distance from the `left` pointer to the index of the last element in the deque that is greater than the current element.  
6. Maintain a running total of all valid subarrays encountered.  

This approach ensures that each element is processed only once, leading to a linear time complexity. Additionally, the algorithm must handle edge cases, such as when all elements are greater than the threshold, or when the threshold is zero.  

When implementing this solution, ensure that:  
- The deque is used correctly to maintain the maximum value within the window.  
- The window boundaries are adjusted properly to maintain valid subarrays.  
- The number of valid subarrays is calculated accurately for each position.  
- The algorithm is both time and space efficient, adhering to the constraints of the problem.  

Include detailed explanations of your approach, the use of the deque, and the sliding window technique. Ensure that your solution is optimized for performance and handles all edge cases.  

P.S. The solution must be implemented in a way that adheres to the problem constraints and is scalable for large input sizes. The algorithm should be both correct and efficient, ensuring that the number of valid subarrays is computed accurately and in linear time.

Iteration 134: Proposed new text for system_prompt: <<Subarray Counting Challenge with Sliding Window and Deque Optimization>>

You are to solve a problem involving the counting of subarrays with bounded maximum values. This is a classic problem in algorithm design and is often encountered in coding interviews and competitive programming contests. The goal is to count the number of subarrays where the maximum value is less than or equal to a given value, or to find the number of subarrays that satisfy a specific maximum constraint.

### Task Description

You are given an array of integers and a target maximum value. Your task is to count the number of subarrays where the maximum value is less than or equal to the target. This problem can be efficiently solved using the **sliding window technique** combined with a **deque (double-ended queue)** to maintain the maximum value in the current window in constant time.

### Key Concepts and Techniques

1. **Sliding Window Technique**: This approach involves maintaining a window [left, right] that dynamically expands and contracts to ensure that the maximum value within the window is within the given constraint.
2. **Deque (Double-Ended Queue)**: A deque is used to maintain indices of elements in a way that ensures the front of the deque always holds the index of the maximum value in the current window. The deque stores indices of elements in decreasing order of their values.
3. **Efficient Maximum Tracking**: The deque allows for O(1) time complexity for retrieving the maximum value in the current window.
4. **Time Complexity**: The algorithm runs in linear time, O(n), where n is the number of elements in the input array, making it suitable for large datasets.
5. **Edge Cases**: You must handle edge cases such as when all elements are greater than the target, or when all elements are less than or equal to the target.

### Instructions for the Assistant

You are to write a Python function that:
- Takes as input an array of integers and a target maximum value.
- Counts the number of subarrays where the maximum value is less than or equal to the target.
- Uses a sliding window approach with a deque to maintain the maximum value in the current window.
- Ensures that the function is efficient and runs in linear time.
- Handles edge cases such as empty input, all elements exceeding the target, or all elements being valid.
- Returns the count of such subarrays.

### Example

Input: `array = [3, 1, 2, 4, 5], target = 3`  
Output: `5` (Valid subarrays: [3], [1], [2], [3,1], [1,2])

### Requirements for the Assistant's Response

- Write a Python function with clear comments and a docstring.
- Highlight **at least two sections** in your answer using markdown (e.g., *highlighted section*).
- Use **at least three letters** in the response (this is to ensure the response is not empty).
- Ensure that **all lowercase words** appear at most **two times** in the response.
- Use **paragraphs separated by the markdown divider: ***`.
- Include a **detailed explanation** of the approach and the use of the deque and sliding window.
- Include an **example usage** with the given example input and output.
- Include a **time and space complexity analysis** of the solution.
- Mention **at least one edge case** and how the function handles it.

### Additional Notes

- The assistant should ensure that the function is **correct and efficient**.
- The assistant should use a **deque** to maintain the indices of elements in decreasing order.
- The assistant should **avoid redundant computations** and ensure that each element is processed only once.
- The assistant should **explain the logic** behind the sliding window and deque usage clearly.
- The assistant should **highlight the key parts** of the code and the algorithm for clarity.

You are tasked with solving a problem involving counting subarrays with a bounded maximum value. This problem is commonly referred to as the "Jacket" problem in algorithmic challenges and is often used in coding interviews and competitive programming contests. The goal is to efficiently count the number of subarrays where the maximum value does not exceed a given threshold.  

The problem requires the use of a sliding window technique combined with a deque (double-ended queue) to maintain the indices of elements in decreasing order. This allows for efficient tracking of the maximum value within the current window. The key is to ensure that each element is processed only once, reducing the time complexity from O(n^2) to O(n).

- The use of a sliding window technique to avoid the inefficiencies of brute force.

Iteration 140: Proposed new text for system_prompt: <<Subarray Counting Challenge>>  

You are tasked with solving a problem that involves counting subarrays with a bounded maximum value. This problem is often referred to as "Jacket" in algorithmic discussions and is a common challenge in coding interviews and competitive programming contests. The goal is to count the number of subarrays where the maximum value does not exceed a given threshold.  

The problem requires an efficient solution due to the potentially large size of input arrays. A brute-force approach, which checks all possible subarrays, has a time complexity of O(n^2) and is not suitable for large datasets. Instead, the optimal solution uses a sliding window technique combined with a deque (double-ended queue) to maintain the maximum value within the current window in constant time.  

The sliding window approach ensures that each element is processed only once, reducing the time complexity to O(n). The deque is used to track the indices of elements in the current window in decreasing order of their values. This allows for efficient updates to the window's maximum value as the window expands and contracts.  

Your task is to implement this optimized approach. You must ensure that your solution is both time and space efficient. Additionally, you must account for all possible subarrays within the given constraints and handle edge cases effectively.  

Your solution must satisfy the following constraints:  
1. Use a sliding window technique with a deque to maintain the maximum value efficiently.  
2. Ensure that the algorithm runs in linear time, O(n), and uses linear space, O(n).  
3. Count the number of valid subarrays that meet the bounded maximum condition.  
4. Handle edge cases such as empty arrays or arrays where all elements exceed the threshold.  
5. Provide a clear explanation of your approach, including how the deque is used to maintain the maximum value and how the window boundaries are managed.  

Include the following in your response:  
- A detailed explanation of your algorithm.  
- The implementation code (in any programming language of your choice).  
- A time and space complexity analysis.  
- A test case with the expected output.  

Make sure to follow the formatting instructions carefully and provide a complete, correct, and well-documented solution.

Iteration 141: Proposed new text for system_prompt: <<Subarray Counting Challenge with Sliding Window and Deque Optimization>>

You are to solve a problem involving the counting of subarrays with bounded maximum values. This is a classic problem in algorithm design and is often encountered in coding interviews and competitive programming contests. The goal is to count the number of subarrays where the maximum value is less than or equal to a given value, or to find the number of subarrays that satisfy a specific maximum constraint.

### Task Description

You are given an array of integers and a target maximum value. Your task is to count the number of subarrays where the maximum value is less than or equal to the target. This problem can be efficiently solved using the **sliding window technique** combined with a **deque (double-ended queue)** to maintain the maximum value in the current window in constant time.

### Key Concepts and Techniques

1. **Sliding Window Technique**: This approach involves maintaining a window [left, right] that dynamically expands and contracts to ensure that the maximum value within the window is within the given constraint.
2. **Deque (Double-Ended Queue)**: A deque is used to maintain indices of elements in a way that ensures the front of the deque always holds the index of the maximum value in the current window. The deque stores indices of elements in decreasing order of their values.
3. **Efficient Maximum Tracking**: The deque allows for O(1) time complexity for retrieving the maximum value in the current window.
4. **Time Complexity**: The algorithm runs in linear time, O(n), where n is the number of elements in the input array, making it suitable for large datasets.
5. **Edge Cases**: You must handle edge cases such as when all elements are greater than the target, or when all elements are less than or equal to the target.

### Instructions for the Assistant

You are to write a Python function that:
- Takes as input an array of integers and a target maximum value.
- Counts the number of subarrays where the maximum value is less than or equal to the target.
- Uses a sliding window approach with a deque to maintain the maximum value in the current window.
- Ensures that the function is efficient and runs in linear time.
- Handles edge cases such as empty input, all elements exceeding the target, or all elements being valid.
- Returns the count of such subarrays.

### Example

Input: `array = [3, 1, 2, 4, 5], target = 3`  
Output: `5` (Valid subarrays: [3], [1], [2], [3,1], [1,2])

### Requirements for the Assistant's Response

- Write a Python function with clear comments and a docstring.
- Highlight **at least two sections** in your answer using markdown (e.g., *highlighted section*).
- Use **at least three letters** in the response (this is to ensure the response is not empty).
- Ensure that **all lowercase words** appear at most **two times** in the response.
- Use **paragraphs separated by the markdown divider: ***`.
- Include a **detailed explanation** of the approach and the use of the deque and sliding window.
- Include an **example usage** with the given example input and output.
- Include a **time and space complexity analysis** of the solution.
- Mention **at least one edge case** and how the function handles it.

### Additional Notes

- The assistant should ensure that the function is **correct and efficient**.
- The assistant should use a **deque** to maintain the indices of elements in decreasing order.
- The assistant should **avoid redundant computations** and ensure that each element is processed only once.
- The assistant should **explain the logic** behind the sliding window and deque usage clearly.
- The assistant should **highlight the key parts** of the code and the algorithm for clarity.

Iteration 142: Proposed new text for system_prompt: You are to generate a response that strictly adheres to the following formatting and content constraints:

1. The response must consist of exactly 8 paragraphs. Each paragraph must be separated by two new lines (i.e., '\n\n').
2. The ninth paragraph must begin with the word "extension".
3. No two adjacent words in the response may start with consecutive letters of the alphabet (e.g., "Apple" followed by "Banana" is invalid).
4. The first word of every sentence must be the word "Jacket".
5. The response must be based on the computational challenge of counting subarrays with bounded maximum values, as described in the first example. This includes understanding the problem, considering the brute force approach, optimizing the solution, implementing a sliding window or monotonic stack, and addressing edge cases.
6. The response must include a detailed explanation of the sliding window technique with a deque to maintain the maximum value within the window, and how this technique reduces the time complexity from O(n^2) to O(n).
7. The response must include a postscript (P.S.) at the end, starting with the word "P.S.", and this postscript must be placed after the ninth paragraph.
8. The response must be written in English and must not include any markdown formatting.
9. The response must include a title, wrapped in double angular brackets, such as <<Subarray Counting Challenge>>.
10. The response must be fully self-contained and must not reference any external resources or prior knowledge beyond the given problem description and examples.

The task involves solving a problem where the goal is to count the number of subarrays in an array where the maximum value within each subarray does not exceed a given bound. The brute force approach involves checking all possible subarrays, which results in a time complexity of O(n^2). However, this is inefficient for large arrays.

The optimal approach involves using the sliding window technique combined with a deque to efficiently track the maximum value within the current window. This allows the algorithm to process each element in constant time, leading to an overall time complexity of O(n). The deque is used to maintain the indices of elements in the current window in a way that ensures the front of the deque always holds the index of the maximum value.

The sliding window technique starts with an empty window and expands it by moving the right pointer. As the window expands, elements are added to the deque, ensuring that the deque remains in decreasing order. If the current element is greater than the element at the index stored at the back of the deque, the back element is removed. This process ensures that the deque always contains the indices of elements in decreasing order of their values.

When the maximum value in the window exceeds the given bound, the window is shrunk from the left. This involves removing the leftmost index from the deque if it is no longer within the window. The process continues until the window is valid again, and the count of valid subarrays is incremented accordingly.

The algorithm must also handle edge cases, such as when all elements in the array are less than or equal to the bound, or when the array contains duplicate values. These cases require careful handling to ensure that the algorithm does not miss any valid subarrays or count any invalid ones.

The sliding window technique with a deque provides an efficient and elegant solution to the problem. It ensures that the maximum value within the window is always known in constant time, which is crucial for maintaining the O(n) time complexity. This approach is widely used in various computational problems that involve maintaining a window of elements with certain constraints.

extension of this technique can be applied to other similar problems, such as finding the number of subarrays with a bounded minimum value or subarrays with a bounded sum. The core idea of maintaining a window and efficiently tracking the required value remains the same, although the implementation details may vary slightly depending on the specific problem requirements.

P.S. The solution described here is a generalizable approach that can be adapted to various problems involving window-based constraints. It emphasizes the importance of using efficient data structures to optimize performance and reduce time complexity.
